<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Chevrolet Cruze</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>The <b>Chevrolet Cruze</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Compact_car" title="Compact car">compact car</a> sold by <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a> since 2009. The nameplate has been used previously in Japan, for a version of a <a href="/wiki/Subcompact_car" title="Subcompact car">subcompact</a> hatchback car produced under a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Suzuki" title="Suzuki">Suzuki</a> between 2001 and 2008 and based on the <a href="/wiki/Suzuki_Ignis" title="Suzuki Ignis">Suzuki Ignis</a>.</p>
<p>Since 2009, the Cruze nameplate has designated a globally developed, designed, and manufactured four-door <a href="/wiki/Compact_car" title="Compact car">compact</a> sedan—complemented by a five-door hatchback body variant from 2011, and a station wagon in 2012. The Cruze was actually released earlier in 2008 to the South Korean market under the name <b>Daewoo Lacetti Premiere</b> until the phasing out of the <a href="/wiki/GM_Korea" title="GM Korea">Daewoo</a> brand in favor of Chevrolet in 2011. In Australasia, the model has been on sale since 2009 as the <b>Holden Cruze</b>. This new generation Cruze does not serve as a replacement for the Suzuki-derived Japanese market predecessor. Instead, it replaces three other compact models: the <a href="/wiki/Daewoo_Lacetti" title="Daewoo Lacetti">Daewoo Lacetti</a> sold internationally under various names (such as the <b>Suzuki Forenza</b> in North America), the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Cobalt" title="Chevrolet Cobalt">Chevrolet Cobalt</a>, sold exclusively in North America, and the <a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a>-sourced, Australasian-market <a href="/wiki/Holden_Astra" title="Holden Astra">Holden Astra</a> (later returning in 2012 briefly as an Opel until the next year, and again in 2015 as a Holden).</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nameplate_disambiguation">Nameplate disambiguation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevrolet_Cruze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Nameplate disambiguation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Cruze_001.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1223" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Chevrolet_Cruze_001.JPG/220px-Chevrolet_Cruze_001.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Chevrolet_Cruze_001.JPG/330px-Chevrolet_Cruze_001.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Chevrolet_Cruze_001.JPG/440px-Chevrolet_Cruze_001.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Suzuki_Ignis#Chevrolet_Cruze" title="Suzuki Ignis">Suzuki Ignis</a></div>
<p>Before the release of the global Chevrolet Cruze compact car in 2008, <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> made use of the name "Cruze" between 2001 and 2008 in Japan. Announced as the Chevrolet YGM1 <a href="/wiki/Concept_car" title="Concept car">concept car</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Motor_Show" title="Tokyo Motor Show">Tokyo Motor Show</a> in 1999, the original Cruze was derived from the <a href="/wiki/Subcompact_car" title="Subcompact car">subcompact</a> <a href="/wiki/Suzuki_Ignis" title="Suzuki Ignis">Suzuki Ignis</a> five-door <a href="/wiki/Hatchback" title="Hatchback">hatchback</a> (known as the <a href="/wiki/Suzuki_Swift" title="Suzuki Swift">Suzuki Swift</a> in Japan).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cruze_price_bruise_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cruze_price_bruise-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Despite the Chevrolet branding, the YGM1, like the production car, was the work of GM's Australian arm, <a href="/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Car_review_-_Holden_Cruze_5-dr_wagon_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Car_review_-_Holden_Cruze_5-dr_wagon-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Along with the styling, Holden executed most of the engineering work and were responsible for devising the "Cruze" nameplate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cruze_price_bruise_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cruze_price_bruise-1">[1]</a></sup> The Cruze came either with a 1.3- or 1.5-liter engine coupled to either five-speed manual or four-speed automatic transmissions.</p>
<p>Manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Suzuki" title="Suzuki">Suzuki</a> in Japan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> GM revealed the production Chevrolet Cruze in October 2001, with Japanese sales commencing the following month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GM_2001-10-22_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-GM_2001-10-22-6">[6]</a></sup> The Cruze was also sold in Australasia from 2002 through to 2006 as the Holden Cruze.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The production Cruze had standard <a href="/wiki/Front-wheel_drive" title="Front-wheel drive">front-wheel drive</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">all-wheel drive</a> optional.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GM_2001-10-22_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-GM_2001-10-22-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Suzuki_Introduces_Ignis_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Suzuki_Introduces_Ignis-8">[8]</a></sup> Chevrolet pursued a marketing strategy that positioned the high-riding Cruze as a light-duty <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">sport utility vehicle</a> (SUV).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> This contrasted with Suzuki's approach with the Ignis marketed as a conventional passenger model.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Suzuki_Introduces_Ignis_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Suzuki_Introduces_Ignis-8">[8]</a></sup> From 2003, Suzuki of Europe began manufacturing the Cruze as the Suzuki Ignis—representing a facelift of the original Ignis, but only for European markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>

</div>
<p>In 2008, GM introduced the Cruze compact car, carrying the "J300" internal designation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Chevrolet_Cruze_First_Drive_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Chevrolet_Cruze_First_Drive-12">[12]</a></sup> This J300 iteration serves as a replacement for the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Cobalt" title="Chevrolet Cobalt">Chevrolet Cobalt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daewoo_Lacetti" title="Daewoo Lacetti">Daewoo Lacetti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holden_Astra" title="Holden Astra">Holden Astra</a>—all unrelated cars. GM phased out production of the Cobalt and its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Badge_engineering" title="Badge engineering">badge engineered</a> counterpart, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontiac_G5" title="Pontiac G5">Pontiac G5</a> in 2010, just prior to the manufacturing of the Chevrolet Cruze was to commence. The first renderings of the Cruze were revealed by GM at a press conference on July 15, 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> with the first official images released on August 21, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cruze production sites include <a href="/wiki/Gunsan" title="Gunsan">Gunsan, Jeonbuk</a>, South Korea;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden.27s_Australian-built_Cruze_surfaces_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holden.27s_Australian-built_Cruze_surfaces-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>, Russia;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shenyang" title="Shenyang">Shenyang</a>, China;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Halol" title="Halol">Halol</a>, India;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gurgaon_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gurgaon-18">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hanoi" title="Hanoi">Hanoi</a>, Vietnam since April 2010 in <a href="/wiki/Knock-down_kit" title="Knock-down kit">complete knock-down</a> (CKD) form,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ust-Kamenogorsk" title="Ust-Kamenogorsk">Ust-Kamenogorsk</a>, Kazakhstan from May 2010;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rayong" title="Rayong">Rayong</a>, Thailand after December 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Caetano_do_Sul" title="São Caetano do Sul">São Caetano do Sul</a>, Brazil from 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Holden's localized <a href="/wiki/Hatchback" title="Hatchback">hatchback</a> version of the Cruze built at the <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth,_South_Australia" title="Elizabeth, South Australia">Elizabeth, South Australia</a> factory from late 2011 joined the Cruze sedan manufactured there since March 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden.27s_Australian-built_Cruze_surfaces_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Holden.27s_Australian-built_Cruze_surfaces-15">[15]</a></sup> GM in the United States has upgraded the existing <a href="/wiki/Lordstown_Assembly" title="Lordstown Assembly">plant</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lordstown,_Ohio" title="Lordstown, Ohio">Lordstown, Ohio</a> to manufacture the Cruze, investing more than <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$350 million</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> At the ceremony of the start of production of Cruze at Ohio, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Reuss" title="Mark Reuss">Mark Reuss</a>, the president of GM's North American operations said, "This is everything for us". It is described as GM's most significant new vehicle introduction into North America since the <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_Chapter_11_reorganization" title="General Motors Chapter 11 reorganization">Chapter 11 reorganization</a> in 2009, and is GM's latest attempt to build a small size car that North American consumers would "buy because they like it – not simply because it is cheap".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT100909_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT100909-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Underpinned by the <a href="/wiki/Front-wheel_drive" title="Front-wheel drive">front-wheel drive</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GM_Delta_II_platform" title="GM Delta II platform">GM Delta II platform</a>, GM has confirmed the Cruze development program occurred under a global design and engineering team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edmunds_2008-07-08_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-edmunds_2008-07-08-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GM_Korea" title="GM Korea">GM Daewoo</a> in South Korea played a leading role in the design and engineering of the Cruze, along with GM's German-based <a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a> division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> This development program spanned over 27 months at a cost of <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>4 billion. A total of 221 prototypes were tested in Australia, Canada, China, South Korea, Sweden, the United Kingdom and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_Cruze_set_at_.2420.2C990_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_Cruze_set_at_.2420.2C990-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to GM, the Cruze's body structure is 65 percent high-strength steel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_comes_clean_on_Cruze_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_comes_clean_on_Cruze-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MacPherson_strut" title="MacPherson strut">MacPherson struts</a> are utilized in the front suspension with a solid <a href="/wiki/Twist-beam_rear_suspension" title="Twist-beam rear suspension">torsion beam axle</a> for the rear, avoiding the cost and complexity needed for a modern <a href="/wiki/Multi-link_suspension" title="Multi-link suspension">multi-link</a> <a href="/wiki/Independent_suspension" title="Independent suspension">independent rear suspension</a> used by some more expensive rivals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_Cruze_set_at_.2420.2C990_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_Cruze_set_at_.2420.2C990-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to GM's global product development chief Mark Reuss, the North America version Cruze is modified from the global platform as it requires reinforcements to the engine compartment because it offers a bigger engine than in other markets and uses torsion beam suspension.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hydraulics" title="Hydraulics">Hydraulically</a>-assisted (electric for North American market) <a href="/wiki/Rack_and_pinion" title="Rack and pinion">rack and pinion</a> steering gives for a 10.9-meter (36 ft) <a href="/wiki/Turning_radius" title="Turning radius">turning circle</a>. Braking-wise, ventilated front, and solid rear <a href="/wiki/Disc_brake" title="Disc brake">disc brakes</a> are employed, both using <a href="/wiki/Piston" title="Piston">piston</a> steel <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brake_caliper" title="Brake caliper">calipers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_Cruze_set_at_.2420.2C990_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_Cruze_set_at_.2420.2C990-30">[30]</a></sup> To counteract <a href="/wiki/Noise,_vibration,_and_harshness" title="Noise, vibration, and harshness">noise, vibration, and harshness</a>, engineers have designed the Cruze with an isolated four-point engine mount and implemented <a href="/wiki/Soundproofing" title="Soundproofing">sound damping</a> material in areas including the front-of-<a href="/wiki/Dashboard" title="Dashboard">dashboard</a> panel, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trunk_(automobile)" title="Trunk (automobile)">luggage compartment</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decklid" title="Decklid">decklid</a> internals, doors, carpet and <a href="/wiki/Headliner" title="Headliner">headlining</a>. Further noise suppression through the use of a triple-layer sealing system in the doors has also been employed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_Cruze_set_at_.2420.2C990_30-3"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_Cruze_set_at_.2420.2C990-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>A five-door Cruze hatchback was unveiled as a concept car at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Motor_Show" title="Paris Motor Show">Paris Motor Show</a> on October 1, 2010. Cruze hatchback sales began in Europe in mid-2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Holden in Australia were responsible for the design and development of the hatchback body variant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>GM unveiled the Chevrolet Cruze station wagon in February 2012 at the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Motor_Show" title="Geneva Motor Show">Geneva Motor Show</a>. Load space ranges from about 500 litres (20 cu ft) up to the window line in the rear, to nearly 1,500 litres (50 cu ft) up to the roof top with the rear seats folded down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevrolet_Cruze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Australasian_New_Car_Assessment_Program" title="Australasian New Car Assessment Program">Australasian New Car Assessment Program</a> (ANCAP) announced in May 2009 that it has awarded the Cruze a full five stars in their independent crash safety test, with 35.04 out of a possible 37 points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The following July, the China New Car Assessment Program (C-NCAP) awarded the Cruze a maximum five stars in their independent <a href="/wiki/Automobile_safety" title="Automobile safety">crash safety</a> test. The Cruze SE 1.6-liter tested scored a maximum of 16 points in side-impact collision, 14.44 in front-end collision, and 15.73 in the 40 percent frontal offset collision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Euro_NCAP" title="Euro NCAP">Euro NCAP</a> released its rating in November, with the Chevrolet Cruze again receiving the full five-star grading. While the Cruze scored 96 percent for adult protection, and 84 percent for child occupant protection, Euro NCAP's figure for pedestrian protection is quoted at significantly lower 34 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In December 2009, the South Korean-specification Cruze—the Daewoo Lacetti Premiere—received the top rating of five stars from the Korean New Car Assessment Program (KNCAP). According to KNCAP, the Lacetti Premiere received the five-star rating in the frontal, offset frontal, side, and whiplash tests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United States, the Cruze received the highest possible ratings of "good" in front, side, rear and rollover crash protection tests by the <a href="/wiki/Insurance_Institute_for_Highway_Safety" title="Insurance Institute for Highway Safety">Insurance Institute for Highway Safety</a> (IIHS), which has recognized the Cruze as a 2011 <i>Top Safety Pick</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Moreover, The <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a> (NHTSA) has awarded the Cruze its highest five-star rating for safety. The score is broken down into maximum five-star results for frontal impact (driver and passenger), side impact (driver and passenger), and for the side pole test (driver). The NHTSA certified the Cruze's rollover rating at four out of five stars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>GM announced in April 2011 that 2,100 North American-market Cruze models would be recalled following a report of the <a href="/wiki/Steering_wheel" title="Steering wheel">steering wheel</a> breaking away from the <a href="/wiki/Steering_column" title="Steering column">steering column</a> during motion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Reports" title="Consumer Reports">Consumer Reports</a>, during its first year, the Cruze scored the lowest in reliability among compact sedans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> ordered a recall on June 22, 2012, for 413,418 Cruze models, manufactured at the <a href="/wiki/Lordstown,_Ohio" title="Lordstown, Ohio">Lordstown, Ohio</a> plant United States, due to a risk of engine compartment fires. The recall covered 2011 and 2012 model year Cruze sedans from September 2010 through May 2012 and affected vehicles sold in the United States, Canada and Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The problem can result when liquids become trapped near the engine and catch fire. In Australia 9,547 Australian-built Cruzes were also recalled but there were no cases of engine fires reported in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> (GM) ordered a recall on August 16, 2013, for 292,879 model year 2011 and 2012 Cruze models, manufactured at the <a href="/wiki/Lordstown,_Ohio" title="Lordstown, Ohio">Lordstown, Ohio</a> plant United States. General Motors told the <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a> the recall was due to a potential intermittent loss of brake assist in Cruze models featuring the combination of the 1.4-liter dual overhead cam gasoline turbo engine and the 6T40 FWD automatic transmission. GM said it was aware of 27 alleged low-speed crashes due to brake issues that may include this particular issue, but it reported no injuries. To address the issue, GM said dealers will replace a micro-switch in the power brake vacuum pipe assembly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of March 28, 2014, GM has halted the sale of 2013 and 2014 Chevrolet Cruze compacts with 1.4-liter engines—models that account for about 60% of Cruze sales—but GM originally didn't say why it issued the order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> GM later announced that the cars were being recalled due to a faulty right-side axle shaft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_update">2012 update</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevrolet_Cruze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2012 update">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Cruze was given a mild facelift for 2013 and unveiled by GM at the 2012 Busan Motor Show, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>. The Cruze received an updated front fascia, with the air vents around the foglamps being redesigned entirely, and the grille and headlights also receiving minor updates. New alloy wheels have also been designed for the Cruze. GM's optional <a href="/wiki/MyLink" title="MyLink">MyLink</a> entertainment system is now offered as well. This model was first sold in Korea, then <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>. It will be later sold in other markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px">
<div style="width: 235px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 230px;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_update">2014 update</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevrolet_Cruze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2014 update">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On April 12, 2014, Chevrolet announced that it will unveil a refreshed Chevrolet Cruze at the 2014 New York Auto Show as a 2015 model, with an updated grille and a more angular shape from the Malibu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px">
<div style="width: 235px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 230px;">

</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>2014 facelift</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Powertrain">Powertrain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevrolet_Cruze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Powertrain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Engines fitted to the Cruze are the 1.6-liter <i><a href="/wiki/GM_Family_1_engine#LXV" title="GM Family 1 engine">Family 1</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Inline-four_engine" title="Inline-four engine">inline-four</a>, a 1.8-liter <a href="/wiki/GM_Family_1_engine#DCVCP" title="GM Family 1 engine">version of the same</a>, and a 2.0-liter <a href="/wiki/VM_Motori" title="VM Motori">VM Motori</a> <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_VM_Motori_engines#RA_420_SOHC" title="List of VM Motori engines">RA 420 SOHC</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Turbocharger" title="Turbocharger">turbocharged</a> <a href="/wiki/Common_rail" title="Common rail">common rail</a> <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel</a>, marketed as <i>VCDi</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> All three engines are coupled to a five-speed <a href="/wiki/Manual_transmission" title="Manual transmission">manual</a> or optional six-speed <a href="/wiki/Automatic_transmission" title="Automatic transmission">automatic transmission</a> featuring <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiptronic" title="Tiptronic">Active Select</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> When the Cruze launched in the United States in 2010, a new 1.4-liter <i><a href="/wiki/GM_Family_0_engine" title="GM Family 0 engine">Family 0</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Turbocharger" title="Turbocharger">turbocharged</a> gasoline engine was introduced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Chevrolet_Cruze_U.S._Spec_-_First_Drive_Review_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Chevrolet_Cruze_U.S._Spec_-_First_Drive_Review-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> North American models fitted with the 1.8-liter gasoline engine have also been upgraded to a standard six-speed manual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Chevrolet_Cruze_U.S._Spec_-_First_Drive_Review_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Chevrolet_Cruze_U.S._Spec_-_First_Drive_Review-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, a new 2.0-liter <i><a href="/wiki/GM_Family_Z_engine" title="GM Family Z engine">Family Z</a></i> diesel engine marketed as <i>VCDi</i> replaced the previous VM Motori <i>VCDi</i> unit of equal displacement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since late 2011, Chinese market models have been available with a turbocharged 1.6-liter engine with a six-speed manual transmission.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevrolet_Cruze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl>
<dt>Africa</dt>
</dl>
<p>The Chevrolet Cruze was launched in the Egyptian market during mid-2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> South African sales of the Cruze commenced in September 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Asia</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20100731_daewoo_lacetti_premiere_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1250" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/20100731_daewoo_lacetti_premiere_01.jpg/220px-20100731_daewoo_lacetti_premiere_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/20100731_daewoo_lacetti_premiere_01.jpg/330px-20100731_daewoo_lacetti_premiere_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/20100731_daewoo_lacetti_premiere_01.jpg/440px-20100731_daewoo_lacetti_premiere_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20100731_daewoo_lacetti_premiere_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Daewoo Lacetti Premiere sedan (South Korea)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Daewoo_Lacetti_Premiere_CDX_sedan_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2776" data-file-width="4653" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Daewoo_Lacetti_Premiere_CDX_sedan_02.jpg/220px-Daewoo_Lacetti_Premiere_CDX_sedan_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Daewoo_Lacetti_Premiere_CDX_sedan_02.jpg/330px-Daewoo_Lacetti_Premiere_CDX_sedan_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Daewoo_Lacetti_Premiere_CDX_sedan_02.jpg/440px-Daewoo_Lacetti_Premiere_CDX_sedan_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Daewoo_Lacetti_Premiere_CDX_sedan_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Daewoo Lacetti Premiere CDX sedan (Vietnam)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>South Korean-market versions of the Cruze entered production there in 2008 as the "Daewoo Lacetti Premiere".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Chevrolet_Cruze_First_Drive_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Chevrolet_Cruze_First_Drive-12">[12]</a></sup> The Lacetti debuted on October 30, 2008, featuring the 1.6-liter <a href="/wiki/Naturally_aspirated_engine" title="Naturally aspirated engine">naturally aspirated engine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> On January 30, 2009, GM Daewoo introduced the turbodiesel engine variant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Inline with the February 2011 renaming of "GM Daewoo" to "GM Korea", the Lacetti Premiere adopted the international "Chevrolet Cruze" name from March 2, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> For the owners of the previous model, Lacetti, GM Korea decided to replace the old emblem to that of Chevrolet for free.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Chevrolet Cruze was launched in the Chinese market on April 18, 2009 as a sedan<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> manufactured at GM India's <a href="/wiki/Halol" title="Halol">Halol</a> factory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gurgaon_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gurgaon-18">[18]</a></sup> Transmission choices were a five-speed manual or a six-speed automatic along with 1.6- or 1.8-liter engines. The sedan range consisted of the 1.6 SL, 1.6 SE, 1.8 SE (automatic only) and 1.8 SX (automatic only). Hatchback models were introduced in 2013 available with the 1.6-liter or 1.6-liter turbo engines.</p>
<p>The Chevrolet Cruze was released in India on October 12, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> It was offered in only two versions: LT and LTZ in diesel form only (<i>VCDi</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>During 2009, there were reports that the Cruze was to become available in <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> with the 1.6 and a 1.8-liter engines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Naza" title="Naza">Naza</a> automotive group in Malaysia has announced that it's expecting to launch the Cruze in the Malaysian market for the first time in the second quarter of 2010 and they are expecting to sell 1,200 to 1,500 units in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Thailand, the car launch in December 2010, built at GM's Rayong facility. Specification levels comprised: Base (1.6-liter), LS (1.6- and 1.8-liter), LT and LTZ (1.8-liter), 6-speed automatic are standard in all models except 1.6 Base used 5-speed manual, with an optional 2.0-liter <i>VCDi</i> available on LTZ variant with 6-speed automatic.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Australasia</dt>
</dl>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2009-2010_Holden_JG_Cruze_CDX_sedan_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1896" data-file-width="3426" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/2009-2010_Holden_JG_Cruze_CDX_sedan_02.jpg/220px-2009-2010_Holden_JG_Cruze_CDX_sedan_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/2009-2010_Holden_JG_Cruze_CDX_sedan_02.jpg/330px-2009-2010_Holden_JG_Cruze_CDX_sedan_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/2009-2010_Holden_JG_Cruze_CDX_sedan_02.jpg/440px-2009-2010_Holden_JG_Cruze_CDX_sedan_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2009-2010_Holden_JG_Cruze_CDX_sedan_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Holden Cruze (JG) CDX sedan</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2010_Holden_Cruze_(JG)_CD_sedan_(2015-07-09)_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2856" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/2010_Holden_Cruze_%28JG%29_CD_sedan_%282015-07-09%29_02.jpg/220px-2010_Holden_Cruze_%28JG%29_CD_sedan_%282015-07-09%29_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/2010_Holden_Cruze_%28JG%29_CD_sedan_%282015-07-09%29_02.jpg/330px-2010_Holden_Cruze_%28JG%29_CD_sedan_%282015-07-09%29_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/2010_Holden_Cruze_%28JG%29_CD_sedan_%282015-07-09%29_02.jpg/440px-2010_Holden_Cruze_%28JG%29_CD_sedan_%282015-07-09%29_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2010_Holden_Cruze_(JG)_CD_sedan_(2015-07-09)_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Holden Cruze (JG) CD sedan</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Australian arm of GM, <a href="/wiki/Holden" title="Holden">Holden</a>, announced at the <a href="/wiki/Australian_International_Motor_Show" title="Australian International Motor Show">Melbourne International Motor Show</a> on February 27, 2009 that sales of the South Korean-produced Cruze would begin under the Holden brand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Replacing the <a href="/wiki/Daewoo_Lacetti" title="Daewoo Lacetti">Holden Viva</a>, the Cruze reached dealerships on June 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The Cruze also became the replacement for the <a href="/wiki/Holden_Astra" title="Holden Astra">Holden Astra</a>, dropped from the Holden lineup the following August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Given the model designation <i>JG</i>, the Holden Cruze was launched with the 1.8-liter petrol engine and optional 2.0-liter turbodiesel. Both engines are mated to the five-speed manual transmission or optional six-speed automatic. <a href="/wiki/Electronic_stability_control" title="Electronic stability control">Electronic stability control</a> (ESC), <a href="/wiki/Seat_belt" title="Seat belt">seat belt pretensioners</a> and six <a href="/wiki/Airbag" title="Airbag">airbags</a> were standard fitment across the range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_comes_clean_on_Cruze_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_comes_clean_on_Cruze-31">[31]</a></sup> Specification-wise, the "CD" opened up the range, finished off with a more upmarket "CDX". The "CD" equipment list comprised 16-inch steel wheels, <a href="/wiki/Air_conditioning" title="Air conditioning">air conditioning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cruise_control" title="Cruise control">cruise control</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Trip_computer" title="Trip computer">trip computer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Power_window" title="Power window">power windows</a> and automatic headlamps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> "CDX" versions add 17-inch <a href="/wiki/Alloy_wheel" title="Alloy wheel">alloy wheels</a>, front <a href="/wiki/Automotive_lighting" title="Automotive lighting">fog lamps</a>, a leather-wrapped steering wheel and upholstery, heated front seats and rear <a href="/wiki/Parking_sensor" title="Parking sensor">parking sensors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Initially a petrol-only model, diesel availability was expanded to the "CDX" trim in early 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>On March 18, 2010, Holden issued a recall for 9,098 petrol-engined 2010 <a href="/wiki/Model_year" title="Model year">model year</a> Cruzes in Australia and a further 485 in New Zealand over a faulty <a href="/wiki/Fuel_line" title="Fuel line">fuel hose</a>. According to Holden, some hoses on 1.8-liter cars had developed a leakage, although no accidents or injuries had been reported prior to the recall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The recall followed a stop-delivery notice issued by Holden to its dealers on March 3 while the automaker conducted an investigation into the matter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2010-2011_Holden_Cruze_(JG)_CD_sedan_(2011-03-31)_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2898" data-file-width="3905" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/2010-2011_Holden_Cruze_%28JG%29_CD_sedan_%282011-03-31%29_02.jpg/220px-2010-2011_Holden_Cruze_%28JG%29_CD_sedan_%282011-03-31%29_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/2010-2011_Holden_Cruze_%28JG%29_CD_sedan_%282011-03-31%29_02.jpg/330px-2010-2011_Holden_Cruze_%28JG%29_CD_sedan_%282011-03-31%29_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/2010-2011_Holden_Cruze_%28JG%29_CD_sedan_%282011-03-31%29_02.jpg/440px-2010-2011_Holden_Cruze_%28JG%29_CD_sedan_%282011-03-31%29_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2010-2011_Holden_Cruze_(JG)_CD_sedan_(2011-03-31)_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Holden Cruze (JG) CD interior</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Holden announced on December 22, 2008 that its <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth,_South_Australia" title="Elizabeth, South Australia">Elizabeth, South Australia</a> production line would be split to commence local production of the Cruze sedan and the Australian-developed hatchback.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_to_build_all-new_small_car_from_2010_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_to_build_all-new_small_car_from_2010-82">[82]</a></sup> Production was originally scheduled to start by September 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> However, it was confirmed in January 2010 that production would in fact begin in March 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The announcement to assemble the car came as a response to the slowing sales of the larger, locally produced <a href="/wiki/Holden_Commodore_(VE)" title="Holden Commodore (VE)">Holden Commodore</a> range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_to_build_all-new_small_car_from_2010_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_to_build_all-new_small_car_from_2010-82">[82]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Australia" title="Government of Australia">Australian Government</a> committed <span style="white-space: nowrap">A$</span>149 million to the program from its $6.2 billion <i>Green Car Innovation Fund</i>, with a further $30 million given by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_South_Australia" title="Government of South Australia">State Government of South Australia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_to_build_all-new_small_car_from_2010_82-2"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_to_build_all-new_small_car_from_2010-82">[82]</a></sup> GM Holden matched both amounts, but the then chairman and managing director <a href="/wiki/Mark_Reuss" title="Mark Reuss">Mark Reuss</a> would not reveal Holden's total investment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_to_build_all-new_small_car_from_2010_82-3"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_to_build_all-new_small_car_from_2010-82">[82]</a></sup> Reuss announced his firm would be considering the utilization of <a href="/wiki/Autogas" title="Autogas">liquid petroleum gas</a> (LPG), <a href="/wiki/Compressed_natural_gas" title="Compressed natural gas">compressed natural gas</a> (CNG), <a href="/wiki/Ethanol_fuel" title="Ethanol fuel">ethanol</a> (<a href="/wiki/E85" title="E85">E85</a>) <a href="/wiki/Flexible-fuel_vehicle" title="Flexible-fuel vehicle">flexible-fuel</a> and petrol/electric <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">hybrid</a> <a href="/wiki/Start-stop_system" title="Start-stop system">start-stop system</a> powertrain technologies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_to_build_all-new_small_car_from_2010_82-4"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_to_build_all-new_small_car_from_2010-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> These technologies, if materialized, would supplement the four-cylinder petrol and diesel powertrain offerings already confirmed by Holden at the time of the announcement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2012_Holden_Cruze_(JH_II)_SRi-V_hatchback_(16599279832).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2512" data-file-width="4301" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/2012_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II%29_SRi-V_hatchback_%2816599279832%29.jpg/220px-2012_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II%29_SRi-V_hatchback_%2816599279832%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/2012_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II%29_SRi-V_hatchback_%2816599279832%29.jpg/330px-2012_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II%29_SRi-V_hatchback_%2816599279832%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/2012_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II%29_SRi-V_hatchback_%2816599279832%29.jpg/440px-2012_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II%29_SRi-V_hatchback_%2816599279832%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2012_Holden_Cruze_(JH_II_MY12)_CDX_hatchback_(2015-06-18).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2856" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/2012_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II_MY12%29_CDX_hatchback_%282015-06-18%29.jpg/220px-2012_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II_MY12%29_CDX_hatchback_%282015-06-18%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/2012_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II_MY12%29_CDX_hatchback_%282015-06-18%29.jpg/330px-2012_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II_MY12%29_CDX_hatchback_%282015-06-18%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/2012_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II_MY12%29_CDX_hatchback_%282015-06-18%29.jpg/440px-2012_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II_MY12%29_CDX_hatchback_%282015-06-18%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

Holden Cruze (JH) CDX hatchback (first facelift)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2015_Holden_Cruze_(JH_II_MY15)_SRi-V_hatchback_(2015-07-03)_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2856" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/2015_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II_MY15%29_SRi-V_hatchback_%282015-07-03%29_01.jpg/220px-2015_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II_MY15%29_SRi-V_hatchback_%282015-07-03%29_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/2015_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II_MY15%29_SRi-V_hatchback_%282015-07-03%29_01.jpg/330px-2015_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II_MY15%29_SRi-V_hatchback_%282015-07-03%29_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/2015_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II_MY15%29_SRi-V_hatchback_%282015-07-03%29_01.jpg/440px-2015_Holden_Cruze_%28JH_II_MY15%29_SRi-V_hatchback_%282015-07-03%29_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2015_Holden_Cruze_(JH_II_MY15)_SRi-V_hatchback_(2015-07-03)_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Holden Cruze (JH) SRi-V hatchback (second facelift)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At a media event on February 28, 2011, Holden unveiled the Australian assembled Cruze sedan in facelifted "Series II" guise,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_Cruze_Series_II_on_sale_late-March_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_Cruze_Series_II_on_sale_late-March-87">[87]</a></sup> otherwise known as the <i>JH</i> series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-First_drive:_Holden_Cruze_reboots_Aussie_small-car_era_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-First_drive:_Holden_Cruze_reboots_Aussie_small-car_era-88">[88]</a></sup> Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Julia_Gillard" title="Julia Gillard">Julia Gillard</a> attended the February launch to drive the first example off Holden's production line before full-scale production commenced in March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden.27s_Australian-built_Cruze_surfaces_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-Holden.27s_Australian-built_Cruze_surfaces-15">[15]</a></sup> Holden has confirmed an initial local content level of between 40 and 50 percent if assessed by retail value, with an aim of increasing Cruze localization over time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Series II styling revisions to the <a href="/wiki/Grille" title="Grille">grille</a>, lower air <a href="/wiki/Intake" title="Intake">intake</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bumper_(car)" title="Bumper (car)">bumper</a> have softened the front-end to bear a closer resemblance to Holden's larger <a href="/wiki/Holden_Commodore_(VE)" title="Holden Commodore (VE)">VE II Commodore</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_Cruze_Series_II_on_sale_late-March_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_Cruze_Series_II_on_sale_late-March-87">[87]</a></sup> Further differentiation from the original has been achieved via the fitment of amber front <a href="/wiki/Automotive_lighting" title="Automotive lighting">indicator</a> lights, jewelled bezel headlamps, remodelled wheel trims, and through adjustments to the lower portion of the rear bumper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_Cruze_Series_II_on_sale_late-March_87-2"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_Cruze_Series_II_on_sale_late-March-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Holden_Cruze_Series_II_Sedan_Revealed_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Holden_Cruze_Series_II_Sedan_Revealed-91">[91]</a></sup> Carrying over largely unchanged is the 1.8-liter petrol inline-four, tweaked to yield slight enhancements in drivability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_Cruze_to_lead_fuel_economy_way_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_Cruze_to_lead_fuel_economy_way-92">[92]</a></sup> When automatic transmission is specified, the 1.8-liter is now teamed with GM's six-speed <i>6T30</i> unit, lighter and more compact than the previous <i><a href="/wiki/GM_6T40_transmission" title="GM 6T40 transmission">6T40</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-First_drive:_Holden_Cruze_reboots_Aussie_small-car_era_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-First_drive:_Holden_Cruze_reboots_Aussie_small-car_era-88">[88]</a></sup> Diesel remains optional for "CD" and "CDX" specifications over the standard 1.8-liter petrol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_Cruze_to_lead_fuel_economy_way_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_Cruze_to_lead_fuel_economy_way-92">[92]</a></sup> Alterations to the 2.0-liter turbodiesel have resulted in an additional 10 kilowatts (13 hp) and 40 newton metres (30 lb·ft) and a slight reduction in fuel consumption for the manual variant, now a six-speed unit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Holden_Cruze_Series_II_Sedan_Revealed_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Holden_Cruze_Series_II_Sedan_Revealed-91">[91]</a></sup> However, the headline change is the release of the turbocharged 1.4-liter engine, dubbed <i>iTi</i> by Holden for <i>intelligent turbo induction</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Holden_Cruze_Series_II_Sedan_Revealed_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Holden_Cruze_Series_II_Sedan_Revealed-91">[91]</a></sup> The inclusion of the 1.4 also brings an upgrade to electric (as opposed to hydraulic) <a href="/wiki/Power_steering" title="Power steering">power steering</a> and affixes a <a href="/wiki/Watt%27s_linkage" title="Watt's linkage">Watt's linkage</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Twist-beam_rear_suspension" title="Twist-beam rear suspension">torsion beam rear suspension</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden.27s_Australian-built_Cruze_surfaces_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-Holden.27s_Australian-built_Cruze_surfaces-15">[15]</a></sup> Linked with six-speed manual or automatic transmissions, the 1.4 is fitted as standard to the new "SRi" and "SRi-V" sports-oriented trims, but is available at extra cost on the base "CD".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Holden_Cruze_Series_II_Sedan_Revealed_91-3"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Holden_Cruze_Series_II_Sedan_Revealed-91">[91]</a></sup> The new "SRi" and "SRi-V" models have their respective badges embossed onto the grille insert, are fitted with their own front bumper design, and feature side skirts, chrome exterior door handles, a rear lip <a href="/wiki/Spoiler_(car)" title="Spoiler (car)">spoiler</a>, and five-spoke 17-inch alloy wheels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holden_Cruze_Series_II_on_sale_late-March_87-3"><a href="#cite_note-Holden_Cruze_Series_II_on_sale_late-March-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Holden_Cruze_SRi_And_SRi-V_Revealed_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Holden_Cruze_SRi_And_SRi-V_Revealed-93">[93]</a></sup> Over the "CD", "SRi" gains a leather-covered steering wheel rim and <a href="/wiki/Gear_stick" title="Gear stick">shift lever</a>, with the "SRi-V" extending this upholstering to the seating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Holden_Cruze_SRi_And_SRi-V_Revealed_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Holden_Cruze_SRi_And_SRi-V_Revealed-93">[93]</a></sup> A heat function for the front seats, <a href="/wiki/Smart_key" title="Smart key">keyless entry</a> with push-button engine start, reversing sensors, and seven-inch <a href="/wiki/Liquid-crystal_display" title="Liquid-crystal display">LCD</a> multimedia unit are also part of the "SRi-V" equipment list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Holden_Cruze_SRi_And_SRi-V_Revealed_93-2"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Holden_Cruze_SRi_And_SRi-V_Revealed-93">[93]</a></sup> This multimedia system integrates <a href="/wiki/Automotive_navigation_system" title="Automotive navigation system">satellite navigation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/CD_player" title="CD player">CD</a> and <a href="/wiki/DVD_player" title="DVD player">DVD players</a>, and a 10 GB internal <a href="/wiki/Hard_disk_drive" title="Hard disk drive">hard disk drive</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Holden_Cruze_SRi_And_SRi-V_Revealed_93-3"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Holden_Cruze_SRi_And_SRi-V_Revealed-93">[93]</a></sup> In mid-November 2011, Holden released the MY12 update to the Series II Cruze. This update coincided with the release of the hatchback body variant and saw <a href="/wiki/Bluetooth" title="Bluetooth">Bluetooth</a> telephone connectivity standard across the range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2013 the Series II Cruze received an update and price drops. The update included rear-parking sensors, a 7-inch touch-screen, suspension adjustments and improved automatic gearboxes across the range along with many other new extras such as a larger 1.6-liter turbocharged engine as standard on the SRi and SRi-V, replacing the 1.4-liter turbo.</p>
<p>Holden will end manufacturing of the Cruze at its Elizabeth plant on October 7, 2016, to be replaced by the Astra hatchback and new generation Cruze sedan—both imported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Europe</dt>
</dl>
<p>European specification variants of the Cruze are offered with 1.6- and 1.8-litre petrol engines, and 2.0-litre and (from 2012) 1.7-litre diesel engines. In mid-2011, with the arrival of the five-door hatchback variant, the 1.6-litre petrol engine received an upgrade from 113 bhp to 122 bhp. Exports from the South Korean factory began on February 24, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>North America</dt>
</dl>
<p>Mexico became the first North American country to receive the car, going on sale for the 2010 model year in late 2009. Imported from South Korea, the Chevrolet Cruze in Mexico replaces both the <a href="/wiki/Opel_Astra" title="Opel Astra">Chevrolet Astra</a> (last sold in 2008) and <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Optra" title="Chevrolet Optra">Optra</a> as the compact offering there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>The US and Canadian version of the Chevrolet Cruze entered limited production at <a href="/wiki/Lordstown,_Ohio" title="Lordstown, Ohio">Lordstown, Ohio</a>, in July 2010 as a 2011 model, replacing the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Cobalt" title="Chevrolet Cobalt">Chevrolet Cobalt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Full production began September 8, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> For these markets, the Cruze utilizes a more advanced <a href="/wiki/Watt%27s_linkage" title="Watt's linkage">Watts Z-link</a> rear suspension from the <a href="/wiki/Opel_Astra" title="Opel Astra">Opel Astra</a> (J).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Offered in LS, LT, LTZ, and Eco trim lines,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Chevrolet_Cruze_Revealed_Ahead_of_LA_Auto_Show_Debut_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Chevrolet_Cruze_Revealed_Ahead_of_LA_Auto_Show_Debut-103">[103]</a></sup> both the 1.8-liter and the turbocharged 1.4-liter engines are offered, coupled with either a six-speed manual or automatic transmission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011_Chevrolet_Cruze_Revealed_Ahead_of_LA_Auto_Show_Debut_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Chevrolet_Cruze_Revealed_Ahead_of_LA_Auto_Show_Debut-103">[103]</a></sup> With a starting price slightly higher than most compact competitors, the base model Cruze LS is equipped with the 1.8-liter gasoline engine and comes with air-conditioning and power locks, the higher-level LT and LTZ models is fitted with the 1.4-liter turbocharged gasoline engine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT100909_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT100909-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> For the Eco model, aerodynamic improvements have been made such as an electronically controlled air shutter that adjusts air flow to the engine depending on the temperature, wind speed and tow weight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> To save weight, Chevrolet replaces the space saving spare tire and <a href="/wiki/Jack_(device)" title="Jack (device)">jack</a> on the Eco model with a tire inflator kit, reducing weight by 12 kilograms (26 lb).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>Standard <a href="/wiki/Automobile_safety" title="Automobile safety">safety equipment</a> includes <a href="/wiki/Electronic_stability_control" title="Electronic stability control">electronic stability control</a> and ten airbags, including side rear-seat and front knee airbags not fitted on models produced in the original South Korea facility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The Cobalt's <a href="/wiki/Rebadging" title="Rebadging">badge engineered</a> twin, the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Cobalt" title="Chevrolet Cobalt">Pontiac G5</a>, has not been replaced by a Cruze-based equivalent, due to the Pontiac brand being phased out during 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The Cruze is built on the production lines that were used to build the Cobalt and Pontiac G5 in Lordstown, Ohio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Cobalt production ended in June 2010 and the Cruze started production in July 2010. GM has allocated three shifts to produce the Cruze and it arrived to dealers in September 2010, giving all dealers time to deplete their inventories of Cobalts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>Changes to the North American-built Cruze for model year 2012 include the availability of the six-speed manual transmission for the 1.4-litre turbocharged engine, plus models not equipped with power front seats no longer have the front seat cushion tilt option.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>Starting with the 2014 model year, Chevrolet offered the Cruze with the <a href="/wiki/Ultra-low-sulfur_diesel" title="Ultra-low-sulfur diesel">clean diesel</a> engine option for North America. With a starting price of $25,695, the Cruze diesel 2.0-liter <i><a href="/wiki/JTD_engine#2.0_Multijet" title="JTD engine">Multijet</a></i> engine got 44 mpg on the highway and 27 mpg in the city, while producing 148 hp (110 kW) and 258 lb·ft (350 N·m), mated to a six-speed automatic transmission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> The 2014 Chevy Cruze Clean Turbo Diesel, direct from the factory, will be rated for up to B20 (blend of 20% <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a> / 80% regular diesel) biodiesel compatibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Cruze diesel was the first GM passenger car in the US equipped with a diesel engine in 28 years, however sales were weaker than expected with 2% of US models.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greencarreports.com_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-greencarreports.com-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>For 2016, the first generation Cruze continued as a fleet and rental exclusive model in the United States, billed as <b>Cruze Limited</b>. The diesel model was discontinued, but a new chrome appearance package was offered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>South America</dt>
</dl>
<p>The car was launched and began production for South America in 2011.</p>
