<p>In 2013, Chevrolet had announced a launch for the second generation Cruze in late 2015, after originally being scheduled to debut in late 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-122">[122]</a></sup> The delay is reportedly caused by engineering modifications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-122">[122]</a></sup> The model had been spotted covered in camouflage while being tested in February,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> and October 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Its supposed interior was also spotted,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> while graphical renders were presented by the Carscoops website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The model will be slightly longer than the first generation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese_version_.282014.E2.80.932016.29">Chinese version (2014–2016)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevrolet_Cruze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Chinese version (2014–2016)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Cruze_J400_02_China_2015-04-06.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="825" data-file-width="1300" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Chevrolet_Cruze_J400_02_China_2015-04-06.jpg/220px-Chevrolet_Cruze_J400_02_China_2015-04-06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Chevrolet_Cruze_J400_02_China_2015-04-06.jpg/330px-Chevrolet_Cruze_J400_02_China_2015-04-06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Chevrolet_Cruze_J400_02_China_2015-04-06.jpg/440px-Chevrolet_Cruze_J400_02_China_2015-04-06.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_Cruze_J400_02_China_2015-04-06.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chevrolet Cruze J400 (China)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The new model was first announced for the Chinese market on the 2014 Beijing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shanghai_Auto_Show" title="Shanghai Auto Show">Auto Show</a> and went on sale in August 2014. The four-door model with a <a href="/wiki/Fastback" title="Fastback">fastback</a> design and a low drag coefficient of 0.28 comes with a choice of a 1.4 L (1,399 cc) turbocharged direct injection engine with a power of 110 kW (150 hp) @ 5600 RPM and torque of 235 N·m (173 lb·ft) @1600–4000 RPM, which can be mated with a six-speed manual transmission or seven-speed Start/Stop enabled <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dual-clutch_gearbox" title="Dual-clutch gearbox">dual-clutch gearbox</a>, or a 1.5 L (1,490 cc) direct injection engine with a power of 84 kW (113 hp) @ 5600 RPM and torque of 146 N·m (108 lb·ft) @ 6000 RPM mated to a six-speed Start/Stop-capable <a href="/wiki/Automatic_transmission" title="Automatic transmission">automatic transmission</a>. Both engines come from the new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GM_Small_Gasoline_Engine" title="GM Small Gasoline Engine">GM Small Gasoline Engine</a> family. Weight reduction of 10% is achieved by using very high-strength steels and aluminum alloys. <a href="/wiki/Watt%27s_linkage" title="Watt's linkage">Watt's link</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Torsion_beam_suspension" title="Torsion beam suspension">torsion beam rear suspension</a>, first used on the <a href="/wiki/Opel_Astra" title="Opel Astra">Opel Astra</a> (J), comes as standard. The car comes equipped with a 4.2" color screen radio or <a href="/wiki/MyLink" title="MyLink">MyLink</a> 2.0 infotainment system with a 8" screen, and can be configured with <a href="/wiki/OnStar" title="OnStar">OnStar</a> Gen10 offering 4G <a href="/wiki/LTE_(telecommunication)" title="LTE (telecommunication)">LTE</a> Internet connection with a built-in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wi-Fi_hotspot" title="Wi-Fi hotspot">Wi-Fi hotspot</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_version_.282016.E2.80.93present.29">International version (2016–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevrolet_Cruze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: International version (2016–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2016_Chevrolet_Cruze.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3571" data-file-width="5357" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/2016_Chevrolet_Cruze.jpg/220px-2016_Chevrolet_Cruze.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/2016_Chevrolet_Cruze.jpg/330px-2016_Chevrolet_Cruze.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/2016_Chevrolet_Cruze.jpg/440px-2016_Chevrolet_Cruze.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2016_Chevrolet_Cruze.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2016 Chevrolet Cruze sedan</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%2717_Chevrolet_Cruze_Hatchback_--_Rear.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2182" data-file-width="3258" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/%2717_Chevrolet_Cruze_Hatchback_--_Rear.jpg/220px-%2717_Chevrolet_Cruze_Hatchback_--_Rear.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/%2717_Chevrolet_Cruze_Hatchback_--_Rear.jpg/330px-%2717_Chevrolet_Cruze_Hatchback_--_Rear.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/%2717_Chevrolet_Cruze_Hatchback_--_Rear.jpg/440px-%2717_Chevrolet_Cruze_Hatchback_--_Rear.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%2717_Chevrolet_Cruze_Hatchback_--_Rear.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chevrolet Cruze hatchback</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 2016 North American-market Cruze has a new external design with a new split grille front. This second generation Cruze has a slightly longer length and wheelbase than the one designed for the Chinese market, with different styling cues. The North American Cruze is also powered by the 1.4-liter turbocharged four-cylinder engine producing 153 hp (114 kW) and 177 lb·ft (240 N·m) torque.</p>
<p>The 2016 Cruze comes equipped with both Apple <a href="/wiki/CarPlay" title="CarPlay">CarPlay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Android_Auto" title="Android Auto">Android Auto</a> Capability features. However, only one of their phone brands at any one time can be used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2016, Chevrolet unveiled the hatchback version of the North American Cruze, it will go on sale in late 2016 as a 2017 model.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trim levels continue to be L, LS, LT (now combined into one trim level, as opposed to the previous 1LT and 2LT designations), and Premier (replacing the previous LTZ trim level as the top-of-the-line Cruze trim level). Discontinued are the Eco and Diesel trim levels (at least for the time being).</p>
<p>All trim levels include a seven-inch <a href="/wiki/MyLink" title="MyLink">MyLink</a> touch-screen infotainment system with A/M-F/M radio, USB integration, a 3.5-millimeter auxiliary audio input jack, optional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SiriusXM" title="SiriusXM">SiriusXM</a> <a href="/wiki/Satellite_radio" title="Satellite radio">satellite radio</a>, voice control, and CarPlay and Android Auto capabilities, keyless entry, power windows, power door locks, <a href="/wiki/OnStar" title="OnStar">OnStar</a> with <a href="/wiki/4G" title="4G">4G</a>/<a href="/wiki/LTE_(telecommunication)" title="LTE (telecommunication)">LTE</a>/<a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a> Hotspot connectivity for multiple devices and RemoteLink via an app on the consumer's <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a>, air conditioning, and a 1.4-liter <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EcoTec" title="EcoTec">EcoTec</a> inline-four engine.</p>
<p>Higher trim levels (LT and Premier) also offer features such as the "RS Sport Package", alloy wheels, remote start, keyless access with push-button ignition, a premium sound system by <a href="/wiki/Bose_Corporation" title="Bose Corporation">Bose</a> with external amplifier and subwoofer, an eight-inch MyLink infotainment system with GPS navigation, a power tilt-and-sliding sunroof, and power seats. However, only the top-of-the-line Premier trim level offers heated leather seating surfaces, premium alloy wheels, and other luxury features.</p>
<p>The base L only offers a six-speed manual transmission, while the Premier, on the other end of the spectrum, offers only a six-speed automatic transmission. The LS and LT trim levels offer either a six-speed manual transmission, or a six-speed automatic transmission.</p>
<p>A new diesel-powered Cruze will be available in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> It will have the 1.6L turbodiesel also found in the 2018 Equinox, paired to either a nine-speed automatic or six-speed manual transmission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsport">Motorsport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevrolet_Cruze&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Motorsport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_trio_2011_WTCC_Race_of_Japan_(Race_2).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1103" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Chevrolet_trio_2011_WTCC_Race_of_Japan_%28Race_2%29.jpg/220px-Chevrolet_trio_2011_WTCC_Race_of_Japan_%28Race_2%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Chevrolet_trio_2011_WTCC_Race_of_Japan_%28Race_2%29.jpg/330px-Chevrolet_trio_2011_WTCC_Race_of_Japan_%28Race_2%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Chevrolet_trio_2011_WTCC_Race_of_Japan_%28Race_2%29.jpg/440px-Chevrolet_trio_2011_WTCC_Race_of_Japan_%28Race_2%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chevrolet_trio_2011_WTCC_Race_of_Japan_(Race_2).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The three works Cruze touring cars competing in the WTCC</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Chevrolet Cruze first entered the <a href="/wiki/World_Touring_Car_Championship" title="World Touring Car Championship">World Touring Car Championship</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_World_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2009 World Touring Car Championship season">2009</a> with a 2.0-litre naturally aspirated engine, taking six wins in its debut season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The car has proved successful since its entry, with <a href="/wiki/Yvan_Muller" title="Yvan Muller">Yvan Muller</a> winning the championship in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_World_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2010 World Touring Car Championship season">2010</a> and again in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_World_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2011 World Touring Car Championship season">2011</a> using the new 1.6-litre turbocharged engine. Chevrolet placed first, second and third in 2011, with Muller finishing ahead of team mates <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rob_Huff" title="Rob Huff">Rob Huff</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alain_Menu" title="Alain Menu">Alain Menu</a>. Chevrolet finished 1–2–3 again in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_World_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2012 World Touring Car Championship season">2012</a>, this time, Huff becoming champion ahead of Menu and Muller.</p>
<p>The Cruze also entered the <a href="/wiki/British_Touring_Car_Championship" title="British Touring Car Championship">British Touring Car Championship</a> for 2010 and 2011. <a href="/wiki/Jason_Plato" title="Jason Plato">Jason Plato</a> won the championship for Chevrolet in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_British_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2010 British Touring Car Championship season">2010</a> and finished 3rd in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_British_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2011 British Touring Car Championship season">2011</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> The BTCC Cruze used the 2.0-liter naturally aspirated engine found in the original variant of the WTCC Cruze.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Cruze won the <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Touring_Car_Championship" title="Scandinavian Touring Car Championship">Scandinavian Touring Car Championship</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_Scandinavian_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2011 Scandinavian Touring Car Championship season">2011</a>, being run by <a href="/wiki/NIKA_Racing" title="NIKA Racing">NIKA Racing</a> under the banner of 'Chevrolet Motorsport Sweden' with <a href="/wiki/Rickard_Rydell" title="Rickard Rydell">Rickard Rydell</a> driving. Rydell and team mate <a href="/wiki/Michel_Nykj%C3%A6r" title="Michel Nykjær">Michel Nykjær</a> finished second and third in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_Scandinavian_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2012 Scandinavian Touring Car Championship season">2012</a>.</p>
<p>Chevrolet pulled their sponsorship at the end of 2011 from the BTCC to support the Chevrolet team in the World Touring Car Championship for 2012.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Chevrolet then announced they would not enter a works team for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2013_World_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2013 World Touring Car Championship season">2013 WTCC</a> season. For 2013 <a href="/wiki/RML_Group" title="RML Group">RML</a>, the original builders of the Cruzes, continued to compete without the support of Chevrolet. Cars were also entered by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bamboo_Engineering" title="Bamboo Engineering">Bamboo Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/NIKA_Racing" title="NIKA Racing">NIKA Racing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pepe_Oriola" title="Pepe Oriola">Tuenti Racing Team</a>. Despite no funding from the manufacturer, the Cruze remained the car to beat, even against works teams from <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lada" title="Lada">Lada</a>. Muller won his fourth WTCC title, his third in a Cruze and <a href="/wiki/James_Nash_(racing_driver)" title="James Nash (racing driver)">James Nash</a> won the Yokohama Drivers' Trophy for independent entries, ahead of fellow Cruze drivers <a href="/wiki/Alex_MacDowall" title="Alex MacDowall">Alex MacDowall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michel_Nykj%C3%A6r" title="Michel Nykjær">Michel Nykjær</a>.</p>
<p>RML have confirmed they will build Cruzes to the new set of WTCC regulations for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014_World_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2014 World Touring Car Championship season">2014</a>, which sees the cars increase in power and feature greater aerodynamics. RML aim to build up to six cars. Confirmed recipients include <a href="/wiki/Tom_Chilton" title="Tom Chilton">Tom Chilton</a> who has yet to announce a team to run his car, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bamboo_Engineering" title="Bamboo Engineering">Bamboo Engineering</a> who will run two cars and <a href="/wiki/Campos_Racing" title="Campos Racing">Campos Racing</a> who will enter a car for <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Valente" title="Hugo Valente">Hugo Valente</a>.</p>
<p>The Cruze returned to the BTCC in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2013_British_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2013 British Touring Car Championship season">2013</a> in the hands of <a href="/wiki/Joe_Girling" title="Joe Girling">Joe Girling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tech-Speed_Motorsport" title="Tech-Speed Motorsport">Tech-Speed Motorsport</a>, who loaned the car from <a href="/wiki/Finesse_Motorsport" title="Finesse Motorsport">Finesse Motorsport</a>. The increase in performance of the <a href="/wiki/Next_Generation_Touring_Car" title="Next Generation Touring Car">Next Generation Touring Car</a> entries meant the older <a href="/wiki/Super_2000" title="Super 2000">Super 2000</a> specification cars like the Cruze were now too uncompetitive to compete for wins but were provided with their own category. Now running a 2.0-litre turbocharged NGTC-specification engine, Girling took one class win at <a href="/wiki/Donington_Park" title="Donington Park">Donington Park</a> but missed the second half of the season. The car returned to Finesse Motorsport who entered the <a href="/wiki/Knockhill_Racing_Circuit" title="Knockhill Racing Circuit">Knockhill</a> round of the championship with <a href="/wiki/Aiden_Moffat" title="Aiden Moffat">Aiden Moffat</a> driving. At sixteen years old, Moffat became the BTCC's youngest driver at 16 years, 10 months and 28 days. This was to be the S2000 Cruze's final appearance in the BTCC, as S2000 cars are to be abolished from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014_British_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2014 British Touring Car Championship season">2014</a>. <a href="/wiki/Andy_Neate" title="Andy Neate">Andy Neate</a> entered the 2013 season with a new NGTC-specification Cruze, built by his own team, IP Tech Race Engineering and used an engine built by RML. The car made its debut at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snetterton_Motor_Racing_Circuit" title="Snetterton Motor Racing Circuit">Snetterton</a> and competed at several rounds towards the end of the season. The car has since been sold to Aiden Moffat, who will run the car with his own team for 2014. <a href="/wiki/BTC_Racing" title="BTC Racing">BTC Racing</a> will enter a hatchback variant of the Cruze for 2014, driven by <a href="/wiki/Chris_Stockton" title="Chris Stockton">Chris Stockton</a>. The car was originally intended to be used by Jason Plato in 2012 but RML and Chevrolet withdrew from the BTCC and mothballed the shell. BTC Racing acquired it and were initially included on the entry list for 2013 but the car was not finished in time and never appeared all season.</p>
<p>The first-generation Chevrolet Cruze debuted in the Argentine <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TC_2000" title="TC 2000">TC 2000</a> in 2011, and the second-generation in 2016. <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_Canapino" title="Agustín Canapino">Agustín Canapino</a> won the 2016 championship.</p>

<p>The Cruze diesel was the first GM passenger car equipped with a diesel engine in the American market in 28 years; however, sales were weaker than expected with 2% of U.S. models.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greencarreports.com_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-greencarreports.com-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
